interface for sending a batch of samples to an\n404: // external timeseries database.\n405: type WriteClient interface {\n406: \t// Store stores the given samples in the remote storage.\n407: \tStore(ctx context.Context, req []byte, retryAttempt int) (WriteResponseStats, error)\n408: \t// Name uniquely identifies the remote storage.\n409: \tName() string\n410: \t// Endpoint is the remote read or write endpoint for the storage client.\n411: \tEndpoint() string\n412: }\n413: \n414: // QueueManager manages a queue of samples to be sent to the Storage\n415: // indicated by the provided WriteClient. Implements writeTo interface\n416: // used by WAL Watcher.\n417: type QueueManager struct {\n418: \tlastSendTimestamp            atomic.Int64\n419: \tbuildRequestLimitTimestamp   atomic.Int64\n420: \treshardDisableStartTimestamp atomic.Int64 // Time that reshard was disabled.\n421: \treshardDisableEndTimestamp   atomic.Int64 // Time that reshard is disabled until.\n422: \n423: \tlogger                  *slog.Logger\n424: \tflushDeadline           time.Duration\n425: \tcfg                     config.QueueConfig\n426: \tmcfg                    config.MetadataConfig\n427: \texternalLabels          []labels.Label\n428: \trelabelConfigs          []*relabel.Config\n429: \tsendExemplars           bool\n430: \tsendNativeHistograms    bool\n431: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool\n432: \twatcher                 *wlog.Watcher\n433: \tmetadataWatcher         *MetadataWatcher\n434: \n435: \tclientMtx   sync.RWMutex\n436: \tstoreClient WriteClient\n437: \tprotoMsg    config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg\n438: \tcompr       compression.Type\n439: \n440: \tseriesMtx      sync.Mutex // Covers seriesLabels, seriesMetadata, droppedSeries and builder.\n441: \tseriesLabels   map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]labels.Labels\n442: \tseriesMetadata map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]*metadata.Metadata\n443: \tdroppedSeries  map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]struct{}\n444: \tbuilder        *labels.Builder\n445: \n446: \tseriesSegmentMtx     sync.Mutex // Covers seriesSegmentIndexes - if you also lock seriesMtx, take seriesMtx first.\n447: \tseriesSegmentIndexes map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int\n448: \n449: \tshards      *shards\n450: \tnumShards   int\n451: \treshardChan chan int\n452: \tquit        chan struct{}\n453: \twg          sync.WaitGroup\n454: \n455: \tdataIn, dataOut, dataOutDuration *ewmaRate\n456: \n457: \tmetrics  *queueManagerMetrics\n458: \tinterner *pool\n459: }\n460: \n461: // NewQueueManager builds a new QueueManager and starts a new\n462: // WAL watcher with queue manager as the WriteTo destination.\n463: // The WAL watcher takes the dir parameter as the base directory\n464: // for where the WAL shall be located. Note that the full path to\n465: // the WAL directory will be constructed as <dir>/wal.\n466: func NewQueueManager(\n467: \tmetrics *queueManagerMetrics,\n468: \twatcherMetrics *wlog.WatcherMetrics,\n469: \treaderMetrics *wlog.LiveReaderMetrics,\n470: \tlogger *slog.Logger,\n471: \tdir string,\n472: \tcfg config.QueueConfig,\n473: \tmCfg config.MetadataConfig,\n474: \texternalLabels labels.Labels,\n475: \trelabelConfigs []*relabel.Config,\n476: \tclient WriteClient,\n477: \tflushDeadline time.Duration,\n478: \tinterner *pool,\n479: \tsm ReadyScrapeManager,\n480: \tenableExemplarRemoteWrite bool,\n481: \tenableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite bool,\n482: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool,\n483: \tprotoMsg config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg,\n484: ) *QueueManager {\n485: \tif logger == nil {\n486: \t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n487: \t}\n488: \n489: \t// Copy externalLabels into a slice, which we need for processExternalLabels.\n490: \textLabelsSlice := make([]labels.Label, 0, externalLabels.Len())\n491: \texternalLabels.Range(func(l labels.Label) {\n492: \t\textLabelsSlice = append(extLabelsSlice, l)\n493: \t})\n494: \n495: \tlogger = logger.With(remoteName, client.Name(), endpoint, client.Endpoint())\n496: \tt := &QueueManager{\n497: \t\tlogger:                  logger,\n498: \t\tflushDeadline:           flushDeadline,\n499: \t\tcfg:                     cfg,\n500: \t\tmcfg:                    mCfg,\n501: \t\texternalLabels:          extLabelsSlice,\n502: \t\trelabelConfigs:          relabelConfigs,\n503: \t\tstoreClient:             client,\n504: \t\tsendExemplars:           enableExemplarRemoteWrite,\n505: \t\tsendNativeHistograms:    enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite,\n506: \t\tenableTypeAndUnitLabels: enableTypeAndUnitLabels,\n507: \n508: \t\tseriesLabels:         make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]labels.Labels),\n509: \t\tseriesMetadata:       make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]*metadata.Metadata),\n510: \t\tseriesSegmentIndexes: make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int),\n511: \t\tdroppedSeries:        make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]struct{}),\n512: \t\tbuilder:              labels.NewBuilder(labels.EmptyLabels()),\n513: \n514: \t\tnumShards:   cfg.MinShards,\n515: \t\treshardChan: make(chan int),\n516: \t\tquit:        make(chan struct{}),\n517: \n518: \t\tdataIn:          newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration),\n519: \t\tdataOut:         newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration),\n520: \t\tdataOutDuration: newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration),\n521: \n522: \t\tmetrics:  metrics,\n523: \t\tinterner: interner,\n524: \n525: \t\tprotoMsg: protoMsg,\n526: \t\tcompr:    compression.Snappy, // Hardcoded for now, but scaffolding exists for likely future use.\n527: \t}\n528: \n529: \twalMetadata := t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1\n530: \n531: \tt.watcher = wlog.NewWatcher(watcherMetrics, readerMetrics, logger, client.Name(), t, dir, enableExemplarRemoteWrite, enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite, walMetadata)\n532: \n533: \t// The current MetadataWatcher implementation is mutually exclusive\n534: \t// with the new approach, which stores metadata as WAL records and\n535: \t// ships them alongside series. If both mechanisms are set, the new one\n536: \t// takes precedence by implicitly disabling the older one.\n537: \tif t.mcfg.Send && t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n538: \t\tlogger.Warn(\"usage of 'metadata_config.send' is redundant when using remote write v2 (or higher) as metadata will always be gathered from the WAL and included for every series within each write request\")\n539: \t\tt.mcfg.Send = false\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n543: \t\tt.metadataWatcher = NewMetadataWatcher(logger, sm, client.Name(), t, t.mcfg.SendInterval, flushDeadline)\n544: \t}\n545: \tt.shards = t.newShards()\n546: \n547: \treturn t\n548: }\n549: \n550: // AppendWatcherMetadata sends metadata to the remote storage. Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := t.sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx, mm[i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend:last], pBuf)\n574: \t\tif err != nil {\n575: \t\t\tt.metrics.failedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(last - (i * t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n576: \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. *QueueManager) Start() {\n926: \t// Register and initialise some metrics.\n927: \tt.metrics.register()\n928: \tt.metrics.shardCapacity.Set(float64(t.cfg.Capacity))\n929: \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Start()\n938: \t}\n939: \n940: \tt.wg.Add(2)\n941: \tgo t.updateShardsLoop()\n942: \tgo t.reshardLoop()\n943: }\n944: \n945: // Stop stops sending samples to the remote storage and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n958: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n959: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n960: \t}\n961: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n962: }\n963: \n964: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch: being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1662: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1663: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1664: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1665: sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, func(int) error, onRetry func()) error {\n1982: \tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n1983: \tsleepDuration := model.Duration(0)\n1984: \ttry := 0\n1985: \n1986: \tfor {\n1987: \t\tselect {\n1988: \t\tcase The shard index computed under the old queue count might exceed the bounds of the newly resized queue array.\n\nLooking more carefully at the locking pattern: `start()` acquires a full Lock while `stop()` first takes an RLock to close softShutdown, then upgrades to a Lock to iterate and flush queues. When reshardLoop triggers this sequence, there's a window where enqueue operations could reference stale queue indices before the new queue array is fully installed. Looking at the enqueue function more carefully, it takes RLock, checks if softShutdown is closed, and if not, appends to the queue at the calculated shard index. The key insight is that once softShutdown closes during stop(), subsequent enqueue calls will immediately return false. However, there's still a potential race: between when softShutdown closes and when the new queues are created in start(), any in-flight enqueue operations that already passed the softShutdown check could still be writing to the old queues while FlushAndShutdown() goroutines are flushing them.\n\nLooking at reshardChan in updateShardsLoop, I notice t.numShards gets updated immediately after sending to reshardChan, before the actual resharding happens in reshardLoop. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Ww6geAUdf1nZ552wZFSNSD","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the runShard loop structure:\n1. Line 1580: Receives a batch from batchQueue\n2. Line 1585: sendBatch\n3. Line 1590: stop the timer\n4. Line 1591: Reset the timer\n5. Line 1593-1599: On timer tick, try to send partial batch\n\nNow let me look for the critical issue. During resharding:\n1. reshardLoop() receives new numShards\n2. Calls stop() which closes softShutdown and then starts FlushAndShutdown on all old queues\n3. Calls start() which creates new queues with fresh timers\n\nHere's a potential race condition:\n- When stop() is called, it takes a Write Lock\n- For each queue, it spawns a goroutine to call FlushAndShutdown\n- These FlushAndShutdown goroutines are trying to push pending batches into batchQueue\n- But at the same time, the runShard goroutines are still running and consuming from batchQueue\n- There's a window where samples could be stuck in the partial batch because:\n  1. runShard receives a batch via case line 1580 and sends it (line 1585)\n  2. Then stops and resets the timer (lines 1590-1591)\n  3. But during resharding, ctx.Done() is triggered (line 1563)\n  4. Which causes immediate return and drops all enqueued samples\n  5. BUT - if samples are in the partial batch (not yet in batchQueue), they're stuck!\n\nActually wait, let me trace through the resharding sequence more carefully:\n\n1. reshardLoop receives numShards\n2. Calls stop():\n   - Closes softShutdown (signals new enqueues to fail)\n   - Calls FlushAndShutdown for each queue\n   - FlushAndShutdown tries to push the partial batch\n3. Calls start():\n   - Creates new queues\n   - Starts new runShard goroutines with fresh timers\n\nBetween these steps, the old runShard goroutines are still active. They'll detect ctx.Done() because stop() cancels the hardShutdown context at line 1293. When reshardLoop calls stop(), it closes softShutdown, spawns FlushAndShutdown goroutines to drain pending batches, then waits for the flushDeadline. If samples aren't flushed by the deadline, they get dropped.\n\nThe vulnerability emerges when a batch is mid-transmission through sendBatch() or queued in the partial batch when hardShutdown() fires—the context cancellation can interrupt the send before completion, leaving data undelivered. The more likely scenario involves a batch sitting in queue.batch that FlushAndShutdown attempts to push to batchQueue, but ctx.Done() triggers before the push succeeds, causing the runShard goroutine to exit without ever sending it. The actual problem might stem from how samples are enqueued during the resharding operation itself.\n\nWhen resharding occurs, stop() closes softShutdown, which immediately fails any pending enqueue() calls, then start() creates fresh queues. But there's a race: if an Append() has already captured the shard index before resharding begins, it could try appending to an invalidated queue or hit an index out of bounds. The shard calculation at line 1315 uses modulo arithmetic on the queue count, so if the queues array changes size during resharding, that index becomes stale.\n\nHowever, enqueue() holds RLock throughout—it acquires the lock before calculating the shard index and keeps it until after the append completes. This means len(s.queues) is read and used while protected, preventing the queues from being replaced mid-operation. The softShutdown channel check happens within the critical section, so any resharding that replaces the queues would have already closed that channel, causing the select to return false before attempting the append. stop() closes softShutdown, then releases the RLock. While enqueue() still holds its RLock and checks the closed softShutdown, returning false before releasing. Only then can stop() acquire the Lock and replace the queues.\n\nAfter stop() takes the Lock and updates queues, new enqueue() calls will encounter the old closed softShutdown and return false, triggering retries. The issue isn't immediately apparent from the locking sequence alone—I need to examine how queue.Batch() handles partial batches and whether there's a gap in the synchronization This causes pending counters to become inaccurate and manifests as shards stalling with samples stuck in pending state.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n**Mechanism:** Context-cancellation race condition during batch sending in resharding\n\n### The Bug\n\n1. **Lines 1789-1792** in `sendSamplesWithBackoff()`: When the context is cancelled during resharding, the function returns early with `context.Canceled` error:\n   ```go\n   if errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n       // When there is resharding, we cancel the context for this queue,\n       // which means the data is not sent.\n       // So we exit early to not update the metrics.\n       return accumulatedStats, err\n   }\n   ```\n\n   The comment clearly states the intent: \"exit early to not update the metrics\"\n\n2. **Lines 1645-1649** in `sendSamples()`: Despite the early return, the **calling function always updates metrics**:\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) sendSamples(ctx context.Context, ...) error {\n       begin := time.Now()\n       rs, err := s.sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx, ...)\n       s.updateMetrics(ctx, err, sampleCount, ...)  // ALWAYS called\n       return err\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Lines 1687-1691** in `updateMetrics()`: Metrics are decremented **regardless of the error**:\n   ```go\n   // Pending samples/exemplars/histograms also should be subtracted, as an error means\n   // they will not be retried.\n   s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(sampleCount))\n   s.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Sub(float64(exemplarCount))\n   s.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Sub(float64(histogramCount))\n   ```\n\n### The Race Condition\n\nWhen resharding occurs (**lines 1189-1194** in `reshardLoop()`):\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    t.shards.stop()        // Close softShutdown, start FlushAndShutdown\n    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Create new shards\n```\n\n**Sequence of events:**\n\n1. **Target discovery triggers resharding** - `updateShardsLoop()` sends new shard count to `reshardChan`\n2. **`stop()` called** (lines 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` to prevent new enqueues (line 1275)\n   - Spawns `FlushAndShutdown()` goroutines for each queue (line 1284)\n   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for clean shutdown (line 1289)\n   - If deadline expires, calls `hardShutdown()` to cancel context (line 1293)\n\n3. **Context cancellation during in-flight sends**:\n   - If a batch is currently being sent when `hardShutdown()` cancels the context:\n     - `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` returns with `context.Canceled` (line 1792)\n     - `sendSamples()` still calls `updateMetrics()` (line 1648)\n     - `pendingSamples` counter is decremented (line 1689)\n   - **But the batch was never sent to the remote endpoint**\n\n4. **New shards created** (lines 1237-1266 in `start()`):\n   - Fresh queues created with empty pending counts\n   - New `runShard()` goroutines start with new context\n   - Enqueued counters reset to 0 (line 1256)\n\n5. **Partial batches lost**:\n   - Partial batches in `queue.batch` never get sent\n   - They're lost when `FlushAndShutdown()` fails to enqueue them before hard shutdown\n   - Their samples were already decremented from `pendingSamples` (incorrectly)\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n| Component | Location | Issue |\n|-----------|----------|-------|\n| Context cancellation handling | `queue_manager.go:1789-1792` | Early return with `context.Canceled` |\n| Metrics always updated | `queue_manager.go:1645-1649` | `updateMetrics()` called unconditionally |\n| Metrics decremented | `queue_manager.go:1687-1691` | No check for `context.Canceled` error |\n| Resharding trigger | `queue_manager.go:1189-1194` | `stop()` then `start()` sequence |\n| Hard shutdown | `queue_manager.go:1269-1305` | Context cancelled in `stop()` |\n| Partial batch handling | `queue_manager.go:1422-1434` | `Batch()` returns partial and allocates new |\n| Flush logic | `queue_manager.go:1447-1455` | `FlushAndShutdown()` tries to enqueue pending |\n\n### Timing Window\n\nThe bug manifests only when:\n1. **Resharding happens during active sends** - A batch must be in-flight when `hardShutdown()` is called\n2. **Timeout expires before flush completes** - `flushDeadline` expires, triggering hard shutdown\n3. **Context cancellation interrupts send** - The ongoing send operation is aborted\n\n### Metric Behavior\n\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` shows stuck value > 0\n- Actual samples never received by remote endpoint (but metrics indicate they were processed)\n- Over time, the counter becomes increasingly inaccurate\n- New incoming samples are processed normally (adding to pending count)\n- But total pending never decreases correctly\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**\n   - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` - Orchestrates resharding\n   - `shards.stop()` / `shards.start()` - Shard lifecycle during resharding\n   - `shards.sendSamples()` - Sends batches and updates metrics\n   - `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` - Handles context cancellation\n   - `updateMetrics()` - Updates pending sample counters\n\n2. **`storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go`**\n   - Test case `TestBlockingWriteClient` (line 1312-1316) shows context being used for cancellation\n   - Potentially missing test for `context.Canceled` in `sendSamples()`\n\n3. **Metrics Affected**\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_exemplars_pending`\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_histograms_pending`\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` (might be double-counted)\n\n---\n\n## Why the Issue is Intermittent\n\nThe race condition only manifests when **all three conditions occur simultaneously**:\n\n1. **Resharding is triggered** while targets are changing (target discovery events)\n2. **Batches are in-flight** to the remote endpoint at the exact moment of resharding\n3. **`flushDeadline` expires** before pending batches can be flushed (default 30s as per `MinBackoff` config)\n\nNetwork latency and remote endpoint response time directly affect probability:\n- Slow remote endpoint → higher likelihood of in-flight batches during resharding\n- High resharding frequency → more opportunities for collision\n- Partial failures/retries → increase timeout likelihood\n\n---\n\n## Diagnostic Steps to Confirm Root Cause\n\n1. **Enable debug logging in queue_manager**:\n   ```\n   log level=debug\n   ```\n   Watch for \"Resharding\" and \"Remote Send Batch\" log entries timing alignment\n\n2. **Monitor these metrics during target discovery changes**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - should decrease as samples are sent\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_sent_bytes_total` - should increase while pending decreases\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_failed_samples_total` - track actual failures\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_on_hard_shutdown` - non-zero indicates premature shutdown\n\n3. **Correlate logs**:\n   ```\n   level=info msg=\"Resharding queues\" from=? to=?\n   level=info msg=\"Resharding done\"\n   # Check if any remote send errors occur between these lines\n   ```\n\n4. **Test with slow remote endpoint**:\n   - Use `iptables tc` or proxy to add latency\n   - Trigger target discovery changes\n   - Observe if `samples_pending` gets stuck\n\n5. **Check for partial sends**:\n   - Enable remote write response parsing\n   - Compare `samples_sent_total` vs actual samples received by endpoint\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy**: Prevent `updateMetrics()` from being called when `sendSamplesWithBackoff()` returns `context.Canceled`.\n\n**Change Required** in `sendSamples()` function (lines 1645-1649):\n\nInstead of:\n```go\nrs, err := s.sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx, samples, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, 0, pBuf, buf, compr)\ns.updateMetrics(ctx, err, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, 0, rs, time.Since(begin))\nreturn err\n```\n\nShould be:\n```go\nrs, err := s.sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx, samples, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, 0, pBuf, buf, compr)\n// Don't update metrics if context was cancelled during resharding - data was not sent\nif !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n    s.updateMetrics(ctx, err, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, 0, rs, time.Since(begin))\n}\nreturn err\n```\n\nThis ensures:\n1. Samples lost during resharding don't decrement pending counters\n2. Counters remain accurate\n3. Samples are properly retried on new shards post-resharding\n\n**Additional Hardening**:\n- Add metric tracking for samples dropped on hard shutdown\n- Ensure `lastSendTimestamp` is updated correctly even on cancellation\n- Consider implementing a pre-resharding check: don't reshard if batches are in-flight\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4381,"cache_read_input_tokens":77279,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4381},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7473d8c1-8ef3-47c5-a045-84769681a2e2","uuid":"41486b3a-0b4c-44a9-a64b-03dcfbc4b78c"}
